(2011)</td>\n<td>6.3%</td>\n<td>1.7%</td>\n<td>3.4%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Mixed (2001)</td>\n<td>2.3%</td>\n<td>1.9%</td>\n<td>1.3%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Mixed (2011)</td>\n<td>3.5%</td>\n<td>1.4%</td>\n<td>2.2%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>East Asian and Other (2001)</td>\n<td>0.8%</td>\n<td>0.5%</td>\n<td>0.9%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>East Asian and Other (2011)</td>\n<td>5.3%</td>\n<td>1.3%</td>\n<td>2.2%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Christian</td>\n<td>32.4%</td>\n<td>58.8%</td>\n<td>59.4%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Muslim</td>\n<td>18.6%</td>\n<td>3.1%</td>\n<td>5.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>No religion</td>\n<td>17.4%</td>\n<td>15.2%</td>\n<td>24.7%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Hindu</td>\n<td>15.2%</td>\n<td>2.0%</td>\n<td>1.5%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>OTHERS</td>\n<td>n%</td>\n<td>N2%</td>\n<td>N3%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>English as a main language</td>\n<td>69.3%</td>\n<td>93.3%</td>\n<td>90.9%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In terms of <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_districts_and_their_ethnic_composition" title="List of English districts and their ethnic composition">ethnic composition</a>, according to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">2011 census</a>, 50.6% of the population was <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">White</a> (45.1% <a href="/wiki/White_British" title="White British">White British</a>, 0.8% <a href="/wiki/Irish_migration_to_Great_Britain" title="Irish migration to Great Britain">White Irish</a>, 0.1% <a href="/wiki/Gypsy_(term)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gypsy (term)">Gypsy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Irish_Traveller" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Traveller">Irish Traveller</a>, 4.6% <a href="/wiki/Other_White" title="Other White">Other White</a>), 37.1% <a href="/wiki/British_Asian" title="British Asian">Asian</a> (28.3% <a href="/wiki/British_Indian" title="British Indian">Indian</a>, 2.4% <a href="/wiki/British_Pakistanis" title="British Pakistanis">Pakistani</a>, 1.1% <a href="/wiki/British_Bangladeshi" title="British Bangladeshi">Bangladeshi</a>, 1.3% <a href="/wiki/British_Chinese" title="British Chinese">Chinese</a>, 4.0% Other Asian), 3.5% of <a href="/wiki/Mixed_(United_Kingdom_ethnicity_category)" title="Mixed (United Kingdom ethnicity category)">mixed race</a> (1.4% White and Black Caribbean, 0.4% White and Black African, 1.0% White and Asian, 0.7% Other Mixed), 6.3% <a href="/wiki/Black_British" title="Black British">Black</a> (3.8% African, 1.5% <a href="/wiki/British_African-Caribbean_people" title="British African-Caribbean people">Caribbean</a>, 1.0% <a href="/wiki/Other_Black" class="mw-redirect" title="Other Black">Other Black</a>), 1.0% <a href="/wiki/British_Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="British Arab">Arab</a> and 1.6% of other ethnic heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-ons.gov.uk_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ons.gov.uk-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Christians were the largest religious group in the city in 2011 at 32.4%, with <a href="/wiki/Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> next (18.6%), followed by <a href="/wiki/Hindus" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindus">Hindus</a> (15.2%), <a href="/wiki/Sikhs" class="mw-redirect" title="Sikhs">Sikhs</a> (4.4%), <a href="/wiki/Buddhists" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhists">Buddhists</a> (0.4%), and <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> (0.1%). In addition, 0.6% belonged to other religions, 22.8% identified with no religion and 5.6% did not respond to the question.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The city is home to places of worship or gathering for all the faith groups mentioned and many of their respective sub-denominations. In the case of Judaism, for example, with only 0.1% declaring it as their faith, the city hosts three active synagogues: one <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Judaism_(United_Kingdom)" title="Liberal Judaism (United Kingdom)">Liberal</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Judaism" title="Orthodox Judaism">Orthodox</a> and one Messianic.\n</p><p>Leicester is the second fastest growing city in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<p>A demographic profile of Leicester published by the city council in 2008 noted:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Alongside English, around 70 languages and/or dialects spoken in the city. In addition to English and the primary western and central European languages, eight ethnic languages are sometimes heard: <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a> is the preferred language of 16% of the city\'s residents, <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a> 3%, <a href="/wiki/Somali_language" title="Somali language">Somali</a> 4% and <a href="/wiki/Urdu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a> 2%. Other smaller language groups include <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>. With continuing migration into the city, new languages and or dialects from Africa, the Middle East and Eastern Europe are also being spoken in the city.\n</p><p>In certain primary schools in Leicester, English may not be the preferred language of 45% of pupils and the proportion of children whose first language is known, or believed to be, other than English, is significantly higher than other cities in the Midlands or the UK as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-DiversityOfLeicesterMay2008_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DiversityOfLeicesterMay2008-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>Certain European languages such as Polish will undoubtedly feature in current statistics, although their prevalence may reduce subsequently as future generations rapidly assimilate or return to places of origin, given cultural and geographic proximity and changes in the geo-political environment.\n</p><p>Leicester is believed to be the birthplace of the modern standard <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_change">Population change</span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:90%; width:70%; border:0; text-align:center; line-height:120%;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="17" style="text-align:center;font-size:90%;">Historic and projected <a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>As one of the fastest growing cities in the country, the <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">ONS</a> 2014 basis population projections indicate the city will be home to 400,000 inhabitants by around 2035.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Highcross_Leicester.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Highcross_Leicester.jpg/170px-Highcross_Leicester.jpg" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Highcross_Leicester.jpg/255px-Highcross_Leicester.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Highcross_Leicester.jpg/340px-Highcross_Leicester.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2187" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Highcross_Leicester.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Highcross_Leicester" title="Highcross Leicester">Highcross Leicester</a> shopping centre</div></div></div>\n<p>Leicester has the largest economy in the East Midlands. A recent study by emda/Experian estimated the GVA to be \xc2\xa315.3&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Companies that have their principal offices or significant sites in Leicester and the surrounding area include; <a href="/wiki/Brantano_Footwear" title="Brantano Footwear">Brantano Footwear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dunelm_Mill" class="mw-redirect" title="Dunelm Mill">Dunelm Mill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Next_(clothing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Next (clothing)">Next</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shoe_Zone" title="Shoe Zone">Shoe Zone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Everards" class="mw-redirect" title="Everards">Everards</a> brewing and associated, <a href="/wiki/KPMG" title="KPMG">KPMG</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazars" title="Mazars">Mazars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_%26_Counties_Bank" title="Cambridge &amp; Counties Bank">Cambridge &amp; Counties Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santander_UK" title="Santander UK">Santander</a> banking, <a href="/wiki/Hastings_Insurance" title="Hastings Insurance">Hastings Insurance</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Gas" title="British Gas">British Gas</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Telecom" class="mw-redirect" title="British Telecom">British Telecom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_Inc." title="Caterpillar Inc.">Caterpillar</a> (Inc.), <a href="/wiki/Topps_Tiles" title="Topps Tiles">Topps Tiles</a> and <a href="/wiki/DHL" class="mw-redirect" title="DHL">DHL</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city has historically had a strong association with the production of textiles, clothing and shoes. While important companies such as <a href="/wiki/N._Corah_%26_Sons" title="N. Corah &amp; Sons">Corah</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Liberty_Shoes_(Leicester,_England)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Liberty Shoes (Leicester, England) (page does not exist)">Liberty Shoes</a> and Equity Shoes have closed, companies such as Next and <a href="/wiki/Boden_(clothing)" title="Boden (clothing)">Boden</a> are still active in the city. Moreover, in recent years the higher transport prices and longer lead-times associated with <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalised</a> production in Asia mean some textile manufacturers are locating to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Engineering">Engineering</span></h3>\n<p>Engineering Companies include Jones &amp; Shipman (machine tools and control systems), Richards Engineering (foundry equipment), Transmon Engineering (materials handling equipment) and <a href="/wiki/Trelleborg_AB" class="mw-redirect" title="Trelleborg AB">Trelleborg</a> (suspension components for rail, marine, and industrial applications). Local commitment to nurturing British engineers includes apprenticeship schemes with local companies, and academic-industrial connections with the engineering departments at <a href="/wiki/Leicester_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Leicester University">Leicester University</a>, <a href="/wiki/De_Montfort_University" title="De Montfort University">De Montfort University</a>, and nearby <a href="/wiki/Loughborough_University" title="Loughborough University">Loughborough University</a>. Leicester was also home to the famous <a href="/wiki/Gents%27_of_Leicester" title="Gents&#39; of Leicester">Gents\' of Leicester</a> clock manufacturers.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">Shopping</span></h3>\n<p>Central Leicester has two primary shopping "malls" \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Highcross_Leicester" title="Highcross Leicester">Highcross Leicester</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Haymarket_Shopping_Centre" title="Haymarket Shopping Centre">Haymarket Shopping Centre</a>:\n- The Haymarket Shopping Centre was opened on the site in 1974, and was the first to be built in the City, with parking for up to 500 cars on several levels, two levels of shopping with bus station, and it is also the site of the  <a href="/wiki/Haymarket_Theatre_(Leicester)" class="mw-redirect" title="Haymarket Theatre (Leicester)">Haymarket Theatre</a>.\n- Highcross Leicester opened in 2008 after work to redevelop "The Shires Centre" was completed at a cost of \xc2\xa3350&#160;million (creating 120 stores, 15 restaurants, a cinema, 110,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> of shopping space).\n</p><p>St Martin\'s Square and the Leicester Lanes area has numerous designer and specialist shops; several of the city\'s Victorian arcades are located in the same neighbourhood. <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Market" title="Leicester Market">Leicester Market</a> is the largest outdoor covered market in Europe selling a wide variety of goods.\n</p><p>Central Leicester is the location for several <a href="/wiki/Department_store" title="Department store">department stores</a> including <a href="/wiki/John_Lewis_Partnership" title="John Lewis Partnership">John Lewis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Debenhams" title="Debenhams">Debenhams</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Golden_Mile_(Leicester)" title="Golden Mile (Leicester)">Golden Mile</a> is the name given to a stretch of Belgrave Road renowned for its authentic Indian restaurants, <a href="/wiki/Sari" title="Sari">sari</a> shops, and <a href="/wiki/Jeweller" class="mw-redirect" title="Jeweller">jewellers</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Diwali" title="Diwali">Diwali</a> celebrations in Leicester are focused on this area and are the largest outside the sub-continent<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_drink">Food and drink</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leicester_Market_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Leicester_Market_2009.jpg/220px-Leicester_Market_2009.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Leicester_Market_2009.jpg/330px-Leicester_Market_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Leicester_Market_2009.jpg/440px-Leicester_Market_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leicester_Market_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leicester_Market" title="Leicester Market">Leicester Market</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Henry Walker was a successful pork butcher who moved from <a href="/wiki/Mansfield" title="Mansfield">Mansfield</a> to Leicester in the 1880s to take over an established business in High Street. The first Walker\'s crisp production line was in the empty upper storey of Walker\'s Oxford Street factory in Leicester. In the early days the potatoes were sliced by hand and cooked in an ordinary fish and chip fryer. In 1971 the <a href="/wiki/Walkers_(snack_foods)" title="Walkers (snack foods)">Walker\'s</a> crisps business was sold to <a href="/wiki/Standard_Brands" title="Standard Brands">Standard Brands</a>, an American firm, who sold on the company to <a href="/wiki/Frito-Lay" title="Frito-Lay">Frito-Lay</a>. <a href="/wiki/Walkers_(snack_foods)" title="Walkers (snack foods)">Walker\'s</a> crisps makes 10 million bags of crisps per day at two factories in Beaumont Leys, and is the UK\'s largest grocery brand.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The Beaumont Leys manufacturing plant is world\'s largest crisp factory.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Meanwhile, the sausage and pie business was bought out by <a href="/wiki/Samworth_Brothers" title="Samworth Brothers">Samworth Brothers</a> in 1986. Production outgrew the Cobden Street site and pork pies are now manufactured at a meat processing factory and bakery in Beaumont Leys, coincidentally near to the separately owned crisp factories. Sold under the Walker\'s name and under UK retailers own brands such as Tesco,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> over three million hot and cold pies are made each week.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Henry Walker\'s butcher shop at 4\xe2\x80\x936 Cheapside sold Walker\'s sausages and pork pies until March 2012 when owner Scottish Fife Fine Foods went bust, although the shop is temporarily open and selling Walker\'s pies for the Christmas 2012 season.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:StMartins_aglow-large.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/StMartins_aglow-large.jpg/220px-StMartins_aglow-large.jpg" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/StMartins_aglow-large.jpg/330px-StMartins_aglow-large.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/StMartins_aglow-large.jpg/440px-StMartins_aglow-large.jpg 2x" data-file-width="535" data-file-height="409" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:StMartins_aglow-large.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St Martins a-glow</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leicester_Cathedral_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Leicester_Cathedral_panorama.jpg/170px-Leicester_Cathedral_panorama.jpg" width="170" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Leicester_Cathedral_panorama.jpg/255px-Leicester_Cathedral_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Leicester_Cathedral_panorama.jpg/340px-Leicester_Cathedral_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2413" data-file-height="3346" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leicester_Cathedral_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leicester_Cathedral" title="Leicester Cathedral">Leicester Cathedral</a></div></div></div>\n<p>There are ten <a href="/wiki/Scheduled_Monuments_in_Leicester" class="mw-redirect" title="Scheduled Monuments in Leicester">Scheduled Monuments in Leicester</a> and thirteen <a href="/wiki/Grade_I_listed_buildings_in_Leicester" title="Grade I listed buildings in Leicester">Grade I listed buildings</a>: some sites, such as <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Castle" title="Leicester Castle">Leicester Castle</a> and the Jewry Wall, appear on both lists.\n</p><p><b>20th-century architecture:</b> Leicester University Engineering Building (James Stirling &amp; James Gowan&#160;: Grd II Listed), Kingstone Department Store, Belgrave Gate (Raymond McGrath&#160;: Grd II Listed), <a href="/wiki/National_Space_Centre" title="National Space Centre">National Space Centre</a> tower.\n</p><p><b>Older architecture:</b>\n</p><p><b>Parks:</b> <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Park,_Leicestershire" class="mw-redirect" title="Abbey Park, Leicestershire">Abbey Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leicester_Botanic_Garden" title="University of Leicester Botanic Garden">Botanic Gardens</a>, Castle Gardens, <a href="/wiki/Gorse_Hill_City_Farm" title="Gorse Hill City Farm">Gorse Hill City Farm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Union_Canal_(old)" title="Grand Union Canal (old)">Grand Union Canal</a>, Knighton Park, <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela_Park" title="Nelson Mandela Park">Nelson Mandela Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_Soar" title="River Soar">River Soar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Park,_Leicester" title="Victoria Park, Leicester">Victoria Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Watermead_Country_Park" title="Watermead Country Park">Watermead Country Park</a>.\n</p><p><b>Industry:</b> <a href="/wiki/Holy_Cross_Priory,_Leicester" title="Holy Cross Priory, Leicester">Holy Cross Priory</a> (Roman Catholic),  <a href="/wiki/Shree_Jalaram_Prarthana_Mandal" title="Shree Jalaram Prarthana Mandal">Shree Jalaram Prarthana Mandal</a> (Hindu temple),<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Stake_center" class="mw-redirect" title="Stake center">Stake Centre</a> of the <a href="/wiki/LDS_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="LDS Church">LDS Church</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Stake_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Stake (Latter Day Saints)">Stake</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\nMasjid Umar<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> (Mosque),<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a title="Leicester Town Hall">Town Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Guildhall" title="Leicester Guildhall">Guildhall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgrave_Hall" title="Belgrave Hall">Belgrave Hall</a>, <a Abbey">Abbey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Castle" title="Leicester Castle">Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St_Mary_de_Castro,_Leicester" title="Church of St Mary de Castro, Leicester">St Mary de Castro</a>,\n<a href="/wiki/The_City_Rooms_(Leicester)" title="The City Rooms (Leicester)">The City Rooms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magazine_Gateway" title="Magazine Gateway">Newarke Magazine Gateway</a>.\n</p><p><b>Shopping:</b> Abbey Lane-<i>grandes surfaces</i>, <a href="/wiki/Beaumont_Shopping_Centre" title="Beaumont Shopping Centre">Beaumont Shopping Centre</a>, Belvoir Street/Market Street, <a href="/wiki/Fosse_Shopping_Park" title="Fosse Shopping Park">Fosse Shopping Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Mile_(Leicester)" title="Golden Mile (Leicester)">Golden Mile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haymarket_Shopping_Centre" title="Haymarket Shopping Centre">Haymarket Shopping Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highcross_Leicester" title="Highcross Leicester">Highcross</a>, Leicester Lanes, <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Market" title="Leicester Market">Leicester Market</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oadby" title="Oadby">Oadby</a>, St Martin\'s Square, <a href="/wiki/Silver_Arcade" title="Silver Arcade">Silver Arcade</a> area, <a href="/wiki/Thurmaston" title="Thurmaston">Thurmaston Retail Village</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Wigston" title="Wigston">Wigston</a>.\n</p><p><b>Sport:</b> <a href="/wiki/King_Power_Stadium" title="King Power Stadium">King Power Stadium</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Leicester City FC">Leicester City FC</a>,\n<a href="/wiki/Welford_Road_Stadium" title="Welford Road Stadium">Welford Road</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Tigers" title="Leicester Tigers">Leicester Tigers</a>,\n<a href="/wiki/Grace_Road" title="Grace Road">Grace Road</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Leicestershire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Leicestershire County Cricket Club">Leicestershire County Cricket Club</a>, Beaumont Sports Complex - <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Lions" title="Leicester Lions">Leicester Lions Speedway</a>, Leicester Sports Arena \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Riders" title="Leicester Riders">Leicester Riders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saffron_Lane_sports_centre" title="Saffron Lane sports centre">Saffron Lane sports centre</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Coritanian_A.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Leicester Coritanian A.C.">Leicester Coritanian Athletics Club</a>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span id="Panoramic_view.3B_Suburban_Leicester_WNW_viewed_from_LE1_VII"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Panoramic_view;_Suburban_Leicester_WNW_viewed_from_LE1_VII">Panoramic view; <small>Suburban Leicester WNW viewed from LE1 <u><sup>VII</sup></u></small></span></h2>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LeicesterAttenboroughPanorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/LeicesterAttenboroughPanorama.jpg/700px-LeicesterAttenboroughPanorama.jpg" width="700" height="377" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/LeicesterAttenboroughPanorama.jpg/1050px-LeicesterAttenboroughPanorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/LeicesterAttenboroughPanorama.jpg/1400px-LeicesterAttenboroughPanorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2997" data-file-height="1612" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LeicesterAttenboroughPanorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leicester as viewed looking west to north from the top floor of the Attenborough Tower at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leicester" title="University of Leicester">University of Leicester</a>. In the foreground are Welford Road Cemetery and various buildings associated with the University of Leicester, and more distant landmarks visible include the <a href="/wiki/King_Power_Stadium" title="King Power Stadium">King Power Stadium (Leicester City FC)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Welford_Road_Stadium" title="Welford Road Stadium">Welford Road (Leicester Tigers RFC)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Royal_Infirmary" title="Leicester Royal Infirmary">Leicester Royal Infirmary</a>, /New Walk Centre (since demolished)(Leicester City Council)/</div></div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leicester&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(June 2015)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Airport" title="East Midlands Airport">East Midlands Airport</a> (EMA), at <a href="/wiki/Castle_Donington" title="Castle Donington">Castle Donington</a> 20 miles (32&#160;km) north northwest of the City is the closest international airport. The airport is a national hub for mail/freight networks.\n</p><p>Alternatively, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Airport" title="Birmingham Airport">Birmingham Airport</a> (BHX),located 38 miles (61&#160;km) west southwest of Central Leicester, is about a 45 to 60 minute drive and can be reached by train, changing at Birmingham (New Street). <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">London Luton Airport</a> (LTN), about 74 miles (119&#160;km) to the southeast, can be reached in 1 h 30 mins to 1 h 45 mins by road or main line train services. <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a> (LHR) is a  102 miles (164&#160;km) 2 - 3 hour journey to the south by motorway, or rail travelling on <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Trains" title="East Midlands Trains">East Midlands Trains</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">LUL</a>/<a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Express" title="Heathrow Express">Heathrow Express</a>/<a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Connect" title="Heathrow Connect">Heathrow Connect</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leicester_Airport" title="Leicester Airport">Leicester Airport</a> (LRC) is a small airport some 6 miles (10&#160;km) east of Leicester City Centre and does not currently operate scheduled services.\n</p><p>Note: distances from Every Street, Leicester LE1 <u><sup>VI</sup></u>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">Buses</span></h3>\n<p>Leicester has two main bus stations: <a href="/wiki/St_Margaret%27s_Bus_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="St Margaret&#39;s Bus Station">St Margaret\'s Bus Station</a> and the new and re-commissioned (May 2016) Haymarket Bus Station.\n</p><p>There are three permanent <a href="/wiki/Park_and_Ride" class="mw-redirect" title="Park and Ride">Park and Ride</a> sites at Meynells Gorse (Leicester Forest East), Birstall and Enderby; buses operate every 15 mins from all sites. The park and ride services are branded as quicksilver shuttle and are contracted to Roberts Coaches from the <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_Council" title="Leicester City Council">City Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leicestershire_County_Council" title="Leicestershire County Council">County Council</a>, buses use a purpose built terminal near St. Nicholas Circle.\n</p><p>The main bus operators for Leicester and the surrounding area are <a href="/wiki/Arriva_Fox_County" title="Arriva Fox County">Arriva Fox County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Centrebus" title="Centrebus">Centrebus</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_Leicester" title="First Leicester">First Leicester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arriva_Midlands" title="Arriva Midlands">Hinckley Bus (Part of Arriva Midlands)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kinchbus" title="Kinchbus">Kinchbus</a>, Leicester Bus, and <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_in_Northants" class="mw-redirect" title="Stagecoach in Northants">Stagecoach Midlands</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Cycle_Network">National Cycle Network</span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/National_Cycle_Network" title="National Cycle Network">National Cycle Network</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Cycle_Route_6" title="National Cycle Route 6">Route 6</a> passes through Leicestershire along with other secondary routes. The <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Bike_Park" title="Leicester Bike Park">Leicester Bike Park</a> is in Town Hall Square. \'Cycle Works\' Bike Mechanic Training Centre is in Wellington Street Adult Education Centre and former Central Lending Library.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainline_rail">Mainline rail</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leicester_Railway_Station_from_south.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Leicester_Railway_Station_from_south.jpg/220px-Leicester_Railway_Station_from_south.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Leicester_Railway_Station_from_south.jpg/330px-Leicester_Railway_Station_from_south.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Leicester_Railway_Station_from_south.jpg/440px-Leicester_Railway_Station_from_south.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3892" data-file-height="2605" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leicester_Railway_Station_from_south.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leicester_railway_station" title="Leicester railway station">Leicester railway station</a> lies on the eastern side of the city centre on the <a href="/wiki/A6_road_(Great_Britain)" class="mw-redirect" title="A6 road (Great Britain)">A6</a> London Road.</div></div></div>\n<p>The rail network is of growing importance in Leicester, and with the start of <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a> international services from <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">London St Pancras International</a> in November 2007 <a href="/wiki/Leicester_railway_station" title="Leicester railway station">Leicester railway station</a> has gained connections at St Pancras station to Lille, Brussels and Paris onwards.\n</p><p>InterCity services are operated by <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Trains" title="East Midlands Trains">East Midlands Trains</a>  providing connectivity on \'fast\' and \'semi-fast\' services to London and the south east, and to major cities and towns in the East Midlands and Yorkshire in addition to providing local services within the East Midlands region. Trans-regional services to the <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_(region)" title="West Midlands (region)">West Midlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Anglia" title="East Anglia">East Anglia</a> are provided by <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a>, enabling connexions at nearby Nuneaton onto the West Coast mainline and at Peterborough with the East Coast mainline.\n</p><p>The 99 miles (159&#160;km) from <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Railway_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Leicester Railway Station">Leicester Railway Station</a> to <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">London St Pancras International</a> on the Midland Main Line, are covered in an average of 1h 25m during the morning peak, with journey times as low as 1h 06m later in the day. Transfers onto <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> or <a href="/wiki/Thameslink_(route)" class="mw-redirect" title="Thameslink (route)">Thameslink</a> train services to London City or West End add another 15 to 25 minutes to the journey time and to Canary Wharf, double. The journey time to <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a> is around one hour, with Leeds and York taking approximately two. <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham</a> is 50 minutes away and <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_railway_station" title="Cambridge railway station">Cambridge</a> via <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_railway_station" title="Peterborough railway station">Peterborough</a> can be reached in around 1 hour 55m with further direct services available onto Stansted Airport in north Essex.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Central_Railway">Great Central Railway</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Great_Central_Railway" title="Great Central Railway">Great Central Railway</a></div>\n<p>The decommissioned <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Central_railway_station" title="Leicester Central railway station">Leicester Central railway station</a> is on the late Victorian Great Central Railway line that ran from London Marylebone northwards. <a href="/wiki/Beeching_cuts" title="Beeching cuts">Beeching cuts</a> closed the route in the late 1960s. A preserved section, however, remains operational in the East Midlands centred on Loughborough Great Central railway station providing touristic services through central Leicestershire<i>,</i> passing Swithland Reservoir on to the <a href="/wiki/Leicester_North_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Leicester North railway station">Leicester North railway station</a> terminus.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span></h3>\n<p>Leicester is at the midpoint; Junctions 21, 21A and 22, of the primary English north/south <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1 motorway</a> between London and Leeds/York. This is where the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1 motorway</a> transects with one of the primary northeast/southwest routes; the <a href="/wiki/M69_motorway" title="M69 motorway">M69 motorway</a>/<a href="/wiki/A46_road" title="A46 road">A46</a> corridor linking to the <a href="/wiki/A1_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A1 road">A1</a> and <a href="/wiki/M6_motorway" title="M6 motorway">M6 motorway</a> at Newark-on-Trent and Coventry respectively. The <a href="/wiki/M42_motorway" title="M42 motorway">M42 motorway</a> towards <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Airport" title="Birmingham Airport">Birmingham Airport</a> terminates in <a href="/wiki/North_West_Leicestershire" title="North West Leicestershire">North West Leicestershire</a> some 12 miles (19&#160;km) west northwest of the Leicester urban area.\n</p><p>Leicester is at the nexus of the A6/(A14), A50, A47 and A607 trunk roads and A426 and A5199 primary routes.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Leicester" title="List of schools in Leicester">List of schools in Leicester</a></div>\n<p>Leicester is home to a number of comprehensive schools and independent schools. There are three sixth form colleges, all of which were previously grammar schools.\n</p><p>The Leicester City <a href="/wiki/Local_Education_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Local Education Authority">Local Education Authority</a> initially had a troubled history when formed in 1997 as part of the local government reorganisation \xe2\x80\x93 a 1999 <a href="/wiki/Ofsted" title="Ofsted">Ofsted</a> inspection found "few strengths and many weaknesses", although there has been considerable improvement since then.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tudor_Grange_Samworth_Academy" title="Tudor Grange Samworth Academy">Tudor Grange Samworth Academy</a> an <a href="/wiki/Academy_(English_school)" title="Academy (English school)">academy</a> whose catchment area includes the Saffron and Eyres Monsell estates, was co-sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> and David Samworth, chairman of Samworth Brothers pasty makers.\n</p><p>Under the "Building Schools for the Future" project, Leicester City Council has contracted with developers Miller Consortium for \xc2\xa3315&#160;million to rebuild <a href="/wiki/Beaumont_Leys_School" title="Beaumont Leys School">Beaumont Leys School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judgemeadow_Community_College" title="Judgemeadow Community College">Judgemeadow Community College</a>, the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Leicester_College" title="City of Leicester College">City of Leicester College</a> in Evington, and <a href="/wiki/Soar_Valley_College" title="Soar Valley College">Soar Valley College</a> in Rushey Mead, and to refurbish Fullhurst Community College in Braunstone.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leicester City Council underwent a major reorganisation of children\'s services in 2006, creating a new Children and Young People\'s Services department.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary">Tertiary</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a Gateway">Magazine Gateway</a> and <a href="/wiki/De_Montfort_University" title="De Montfort University">De Montfort University</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Aston" title="Hugh Aston">Hugh Aston</a> building.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Leicester is home to two universities, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leicester" title="University of Leicester">University of Leicester</a>, which attained its <a href="/wiki/Royal_Charter" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Charter">Royal Charter</a> in 1957 and was ranked 12th by the 2009 Complete University Guide,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/De_Montfort_University" title="De Montfort University">De Montfort University</a>, which opened in 1969 as <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Polytechnic" class="mw-redirect" title="Leicester Polytechnic">Leicester Polytechnic</a> and achieved university status in 1992.\n</p><p>It is also home to the <a href="/wiki/National_Space_Centre" title="National Space Centre">National Space Centre</a> off Abbey Lane, due in part to the University of Leicester being one of the few universities in the UK to specialise in space sciences.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Curve_Leicester_full_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Curve_Leicester_full_panorama.jpg/220px-Curve_Leicester_full_panorama.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Curve_Leicester_full_panorama.jpg/330px-Curve_Leicester_full_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Curve_Leicester_full_panorama.jpg/440px-Curve_Leicester_full_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3261" data-file-height="2028" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Curve_Leicester_full_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Curve_(theatre)" title="Curve (theatre)">Curve</a> theatre</div></div></div>\n<p>The city hosts annually a <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Caribbean_Carnival" title="Leicester Caribbean Carnival">Caribbean Carnival and parade</a> (the largest in the UK outside London), <a href="/wiki/Diwali" title="Diwali">Diwali</a> celebrations, the largest comedy festival in the UK <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Comedy_Festival" title="Leicester Comedy Festival">Leicester Comedy Festival</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Pride_Parade" class="mw-redirect" title="Pride Parade">Pride Parade</a> (<a href="/wiki/Leicester_Pride" title="Leicester Pride">Leicester Pride</a>). Belgrave Road, not far from the city centre, is colloquially known as "The Golden Mile" because of the number of Jewellers.\n</p><p>The Leicester International Short Film Festival is an annual event; it commenced in 1996 under the banner title of "Seconds Out". It has become one of the most important short film festivals in the UK and usually runs in early November, with venues including the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Square" title="Phoenix Square">Phoenix Square</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Phoenix_Square_Leicester.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Phoenix_Square_Leicester.jpg/150px-Phoenix_Square_Leicester.jpg" width="150" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Phoenix_Square_Leicester.jpg/225px-Phoenix_Square_Leicester.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Phoenix_Square_Leicester.jpg/300px-Phoenix_Square_Leicester.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2421" data-file-height="3616" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Phoenix_Square_Leicester.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Square" title="Phoenix Square">Phoenix Square</a> cinema and media complex</div></div></div>\n<p>Notable arts venues in the city include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Curve_Theatre,_Leicester" class="mw-redirect" title="Curve Theatre, Leicester">Curve</a>: Purpose-designed performing arts centre, designed by <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Vi%C3%B1oly" title="Rafael Vi\xc3\xb1oly">Rafael Vi\xc3\xb1oly</a>, opened in Autumn 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/De_Montfort_Hall" title="De Montfort Hall">De Montfort Hall</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Haymarket_Theatre" title="Leicester Haymarket Theatre"> Haymarket Theatre</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Little_Theatre_(Leicester)" title="Little Theatre (Leicester)">Little Theatre</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Peepul_Centre" title="Peepul Centre">Peepul Centre</a>, Designed by Andrzej Blonski Architects, the \xc2\xa315&#160;million building was opened in 2005 and houses an auditorium, restaurant, cyber caf\xc3\xa9, gym and dance studio for the local people, as well as being used for conferences and events. The centre has even been host to former Prime Minister Gordon Brown and other senior Labour Party figures for hustings during the deputy leadership contest.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Square" title="Phoenix Square">Phoenix Square</a>, which in 2009, replaced the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Arts_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenix Arts Centre">Phoenix Arts Centre</a>.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Sue_Townsend_Theatre" title="Sue Townsend Theatre">Sue Townsend Theatre</a> - which opened in the former Phoenix Arts Centre.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Leicester_Guildhall" title="Leicester Guildhall">The Guildhall</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_in_Leicester" title="Music in Leicester">Music in Leicester</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span></h3>\n<p>Leicester is the setting for the fictional diaries of <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Mole" title="Adrian Mole">Adrian Mole</a>, created by <a href="/wiki/Sue_Townsend" title="Sue Townsend">Sue Townsend</a>. In the early books he lives in a suburb of Leicester and attends a local school where he first meets "the love of his life", Pandora Braithwaite.\n</p><p>After a period of years spent working in Oxford and London Mole returns to Leicester and gets a job in a second-hand bookshop and a flat in an "upmarket" development on a swan-infested waterfront which is a barely disguised representation of the area near to St. Nicholas Circle. Vastly in debt he is forced to move to the fictional village of Mangold Parva. The local (fictional) <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">MP</a> for the town of Ashby de la Zouch is none other than his old flame Pandora Braithwaite.\n</p><p>Leicester is the setting for <a href="/wiki/Rod_Duncan" title="Rod Duncan">Rod Duncan</a>\'s novels, the Fall of the Gas-Lit Empire series and the Riot trilogy.\n</p><p>Leicester and the surrounding county are settings for several <a href="/wiki/Graham_Joyce" title="Graham Joyce">Graham Joyce</a> novels, including <i>Dark Sister</i>, <i>The Limits of Enchantment</i> and <i>Some Kind of Fairy Tale</i>.\n</p><p>The Clarendon Park and New Walk areas of the city, along with an unnamed Charnwood village ("vaguely based upon Cossington", according to the author) are some of the settings of the 2014 novel "The Knot of Isis" by Chrid McGordon.\n</p><p>Leicester is the setting for the British children book series, <a href="/wiki/The_Sleepover_Club" title="The Sleepover Club">The Sleepover Club</a>, by authors Rose Impey, Narinder Dhami, Lorna Read, Fiona Cummings, Louis Catt, Sue Mongredien, Angie Bates, Ginny Deals, Harriet Castor and Jana Novotny Hunter.\n</p><p>Notable feature films made in the city are <a href="/wiki/The_Girl_with_Brains_in_Her_Feet" title="The Girl with Brains in Her Feet">The Girl with Brains in Her Feet</a> 1997, <a href="/wiki/Jadoo_(2013_film)" title="Jadoo (2013 film)">Jadoo</a> 2013 and <a href="/wiki/Yamla_Pagla_Deewana_2" title="Yamla Pagla Deewana 2">Yamla Pagla Deewana 2</a> 2013.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Leicester" title="Sport in Leicester">Sport in Leicester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City F.C.</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Leicester_Tigers" title="Leicester Tigers">Leicester Tigers</a> have been the most successful English <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> club since the introduction of a league in 1987, winning it a record ten times, four more than either Bath or Wasps. They last won the Premiership title in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WalkerStadium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/WalkerStadium.jpg/290px-WalkerStadium.jpg" width="290" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/WalkerStadium.jpg/435px-WalkerStadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/WalkerStadium.jpg/580px-WalkerStadium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="430" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WalkerStadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/King_Power_Stadium" title="King Power Stadium">King Power Stadium</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City F.C.</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City F.C.</a> are a professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club based at the <a href="/wiki/King_Power_Stadium" title="King Power Stadium">King Power Stadium</a> who play in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>. They were promoted as champions of the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Football League Championship</a> in the 2013\xe2\x80\x9314 season, a return to the top flight of English football after a decade away, and won the Premier League title in 2016, despite the odds of them winning at the start of the season being 5000/1.<sup id="cite_ref-WillHill_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WillHill-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TelegraphBookies_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TelegraphBookies-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Liabilities_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liabilities-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leicester_Riders" title="Leicester Riders">Leicester Riders</a> are the oldest professional <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> team in the country. In 2016, they moved into the new Charter Street Leicester Community Sports Arena.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leicestershire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Leicestershire County Cricket Club">Leicestershire County Cricket Club</a> who are a professional cricket club based at Grace Road, Leicester currently play in the second tier of the county championship.They won the County Championship in 1996 and 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span></h2>\n<p>In the public sector, <a href="/wiki/University_Hospitals_Leicester" class="mw-redirect" title="University Hospitals Leicester">University Hospitals Leicester</a> NHS Trust is one of the larger employers in the city, with over 12,000 employees working for the Trust. Leicester City Primary Care Trust employs over 1,000 full and part-time staff providing healthcare services in the city. Leicestershire Partnership NHS Trust<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> employs 3,000 staff providing mental health and learning disability services in the city and county.\n</p><p>In the private sector are Nuffield Hospital Leicester and the Spire Hospital Leicester.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Leicester_and_Leicestershire" title="List of people from Leicester and Leicestershire">List of people from Leicester and Leicestershire</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_media">Local media</span></h2>\n<p>Leicester is home to the <i><a href="/wiki/Leicester_Mercury" title="Leicester Mercury">Leicester Mercury</a></i> newspaper, and the <a href="/wiki/Midlands_Asian_Television" title="Midlands Asian Television">Midlands Asian Television</a> channel known as MATV Channel 6.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cameraman_and_soundman_filming_police_in_Leicester,_England,_1974.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Cameraman_and_soundman_filming_police_in_Leicester%2C_England%2C_1974.jpg/220px-Cameraman_and_soundman_filming_police_in_Leicester%2C_England%2C_1974.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Cameraman_and_soundman_filming_police_in_Leicester%2C_England%2C_1974.jpg/330px-Cameraman_and_soundman_filming_police_in_Leicester%2C_England%2C_1974.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Cameraman_and_soundman_filming_police_in_Leicester%2C_England%2C_1974.jpg/440px-Cameraman_and_soundman_filming_police_in_Leicester%2C_England%2C_1974.jpg 2x" data-file-width="604" data-file-height="425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cameraman_and_soundman_filming_police_in_Leicester,_England,_1974.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Film crew at work during an "anti-Fascist" march in Leicester, August 1974</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Leicester" title="BBC Radio Leicester">BBC Radio Leicester</a> was the first <a href="/wiki/BBC_Local_Radio" title="BBC Local Radio">BBC Local Radio</a> station in Britain, opening on 8 November 1967. Other analogue FM radio stations are Leicester Community Radio for English speaking over 35\'s, <a href="/wiki/Demon_FM" title="Demon FM">Demon FM</a> which is Leicester\'s community and student radio station broadcasting from Demontfort University, <a href="/wiki/Takeover_Radio" title="Takeover Radio">Takeover Radio</a> is the first ever children\'s radio station in the UK to be produced and presented by children, <a href="/wiki/Capital_East_Midlands" title="Capital East Midlands">Capital FM East Midlands</a> <a href="/wiki/Gem_106" title="Gem 106">Gem 106</a>, <a href="/wiki/106.6_Smooth_Radio" class="mw-redirect" title="106.6 Smooth Radio">106.6 Smooth Radio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hindu_Sanskar_Radio" title="Hindu Sanskar Radio">Hindu Sanskar Radio</a>, which only broadcasts during Hindu religious festivals. <a href="/wiki/BBC_Asian_Network" title="BBC Asian Network">BBC Asian Network</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sabras_Radio" title="Sabras Radio">Sabras Radio</a> broadcast on AM.\n</p><p>The local <a href="/wiki/Digital_audio_broadcasting" title="Digital audio broadcasting">DAB</a> multiplex has the following stations:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Capital_East_Midlands" title="Capital East Midlands">Capital FM East Midlands</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Leicester" title="BBC Radio Leicester">BBC Radio Leicester</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sabras_Radio" title="Sabras Radio">Sabras Radio</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Traffic_Radio" title="Traffic Radio">Highways Agency Traffic Radio</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/XFM" class="mw-redirect" title="XFM">XFM</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Classic_Gold_GEM" title="Classic Gold GEM">Classic Gold GEM</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gem_106" title="Gem 106">Gem 106</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Asian_Plus" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian Plus">Asian Plus</a> \xe2\x80\x93 also known as <a href="/wiki/Hindu_Sanskar_Radio" title="Hindu Sanskar Radio">Hindu Sanskar Radio</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Takeover_Radio" title="Takeover Radio">Takeover Radio</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Smooth_Radio" title="Smooth Radio">Smooth Radio</a></li></ul>\n<p>There are two hospital radio stations in Leicester, Radio Fox and Radio Gwendolen.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_cities">Twin cities</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote and sister cities in the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<p>Leicester is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with six
